98 (Thu 7/22): 30ish miles\n\nWe wake up in the morning to find Bison camped next to us. We eat breakfast and pack up while he tells us about how he accidentally went 8-10 miles off trail yesterday. We then hike out. It's another long day of desert hiking, but we are actually on roads for a decent amount of it. I'm very fed up with the Basin at this point and am wishing any car would stop for a little bit of trail magic. We also start passing a bunch of posts for the Oregon Trail? And the California Trail, whatever that is? Near the end of the day I get to the water source I was planning on stopping at, but unfortunately it's a terrible spot. The next one is only a mile, so I suck it up and hike for another 20ish minutes. I am so glad I decided to go an extra mile because I arrive in South Pass City, a historical mining town, that now operates as a sort of museum/recreation area (Conner Prairie on a way smaller scale, for those from Fishers). There's a bathroom, piped water, and a spot where they let backpackers set up. I roll in at dusk, set up to cowboy camp and hang out with a with a guy cycling the Divide. Bison shows up, and later Nude Beach does as well. Bison warns me that it's probably going to rain and offers to let me sleep under his tarp so I don't have to set up my tent. I agree and help him set it up, which was a good call because it definitely stormed. so hard to explain what a thru-hike feels like - I struggle to find the words to make sense of this experience. Us hiker trash usually end up nodding, not needing words, knowing together this secret world.\n‚Ä¢\nRad and I pushed a single-day Presidential traverse. It was miserably wet, cold, and quiet. Besides the roar of raindrops and swirling wind, it was silent on the mountain.\n‚Ä¢\nI had become accustomed to clouds consuming the White Mountain vistas after that week. We imagined their glory but witnessed only clouds and trees. We had no energy to talk above the wind and we dragged our pruned feet over the wet rocks. \n‚Ä¢\nLater, while hiking up Mt. Lafayette, we realized we were no longer shrouded in clouds. winter action? Don‚Äôt forget your traction! When it comes to trekking winter trails, traction devices are a must to help keep you on your feet:\nüëç Snowshoes are large frames that attach to your boots and prevent you from sinking deep into snow by distributing your weight over a greater surface area. Snowshoes also prevent postholing (when bare boots make deep holes in the snow), which can be hazardous for you and other visitors. Snowshoes should be worn wherever there is significant snowpack, and they are required in the Adirondack High Peaks Wilderness once snow depths reach 8 or more inches.\nüëç Hiking spikes pull on over your boots and are simple to put on/take off, making them easy to pack. Spike versions are best for flatter backwoods outings because they grip icy trails but can be worn down when used on hard surfaces like sidewalks or roads. Versions that use coils or studs aren‚Äôt secure on ice but can help with traction in light snow or on maintained trails.\nüëç Crampons are larger, sharper spikes on frames that attach to your boots. They penetrate ice, making them the best choice for thick ice and steep slopes.\n\nNo matter which is best for your adventure, remember to practice putting on and using your gear in a safe and familiar environment first. Picking the right footwear is just one part of planning ahead and preparing for a safe and enjoyable time outside. \n\n(Pictured, in order: snowshoes, hiking spikes/microspikes, crampons)"}}]},"shortcode":"CY4n75uj1So","edge_media_to_comment":{"count":5},"taken_at_timestamp":1642537522,"dimensions":{"height":1080,"width":1080},"display_url":"https://instagram.fric1-2.fna.fbcdn.net/v/t51.2885-15/fr/e15/s1080x1080/272007306_602668954363648_4750106181481210710_n.jpg?_nc_ht=instagram.fric1-2.fna.fbcdn.net\u0026_nc_cat=104\u0026_nc_ohc=7LjdjEsMqdQAX_Opw4V\u0026edm=AA0rjkIBAAAA\u0026ccb=7-4\u0026oh=00_AT_3eqUc8UeW3ki-CS6H-mDnYrYaubh7AldLMIFP9sCuPQ\u0026oe=61F44505\u0026_nc_sid=d997c6","edge_liked_by":{"count":912},"owner":{"id":"3056106644"},"thumbnail_src":"https://instagram.fric1-2.fna.fbcdn.net/v/t51.2885-15/sh0.08/e35/s640x640/272007306_602668954363648_4750106181481210710_n.jpg?_nc_ht=instagram.fric1-2.fna.fbcdn.net\u0026_nc_cat=104\u0026_nc_ohc=7LjdjEsMqdQAX_Opw4V\u0026edm=AA0rjkIBAAAA\u0026ccb=7-4\u0026oh=00_AT9i9cQ9U-oVnd8olVUTfhonlQMx-vDFYuuqG7mujpcV1A\u0026oe=61F33C4E\u0026_nc_sid=d997c6","thumbnail_resources":[{"src":"https://instagram.fric1-2.fna.fbcdn.net/v/t51.2885-15/e15/s150x150/272007306_602668954363648_4750106181481210710_n.jpg?_nc_ht=instagram.fric1-2.fna.fbcdn.net\u0026_nc_cat=104\u0026_nc_ohc=7LjdjEsMqdQAX_Opw4V\u0026edm=AA0rjkIBAAAA\u0026ccb=7-4\u0026oh=00_AT8LVadMk9nHFX92lG5ezMbNpl9DGeoxDdaTvAxhwsE7Fg\u0026oe=61F2CD31\u0026_nc_sid=d997c6","config_width":150,"config_height":150},{"src":"https://instagram.fric1-2.fna.fbcdn.net/v/t51.2885-15/e15/s240x240/272007306_602668954363648_4750106181481210710_n.jpg?_nc_ht=instagram.fric1-2.fna.fbcdn.net\u0026_nc_cat=104\u0026_nc_ohc=7LjdjEsMqdQAX_Opw4V\u0026edm=AA0rjkIBAAAA\u0026ccb=7-4\u0026oh=00_AT-AHz4ZUeBX_N_1R4qXNOSgdxN9PBQdq-Rs2kM2oRiE6g\u0026oe=61F2F037\u0026_nc_sid=d997c6","config_width":240,"config_height":240},{"src":"https://instagram.fric1-2.fna.fbcdn.net/v/t51.2885-15/e15/s320x320/272007306_602668954363648_4750106181481210710_n.jpg?_nc_ht=instagram.fric1-2.fna.fbcdn.net\u0026_nc_cat=104\u0026_nc_ohc=7LjdjEsMqdQAX_Opw4V\u0026edm=AA0rjkIBAAAA\u0026ccb=7-4\u0026oh=00_AT9juQQ3_Z They're planning on walking into the night, but Nude Beach and I stop and set up camp there. Sharing Respect ‚Üü\n‚Üü\nI‚Äôm deeply concerned about current trends wherein some choose to vandalize or otherwise destroy public lands, national parks, and/or sacred Native American spaces. This week‚Äôs episode in @bigbendnps is no exception. Why do some among us behave so irresponsibly?\n‚Üü\nOne theory I‚Äôm willing to test states that our rash of recent infractions are simply due to the percentages. Since COVID forced so many indoors for so long, a higher number of people than before recreate outdoors upon emergence from lock-down. These large numbers also translate into a higher number (but equal %) of yo-yos spending time in campgrounds, national parks, and on hiking trails. More people, more dupewads. Thankfully, I actually noticed far fewer people on our local trails in 2021 than in 2020, so if this percentage play really does correlate with these increases in irresponsible behavior, then I‚Äôm satisfied that as this crazy world eventually returns to ‚Äúnormal,‚Äù the crowds and number of bozos will eventually diminish.\n‚Üü\nAnother theory I have is that ubiquitous cameras and closed-network sharing are to blame. While it can be easy to throw rocks at online social media as the root of modern evil, I think the problem is more elegant than that. The fact is, we simply don‚Äôt see that many idiots bragging online about their heinous acts of destruction. If and when the morons do take to social media for their public flaunting, such acts often get quickly shamed, rather than celebrated. Nevertheless, because every pocket now carries a camera, those troubled enough to vandalize also have the effortless ability to record their diabolical deeds; not for the world to see and celebrate,
